      <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.20.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20">
        <eq id="p1.1.m1.1.8.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.8"/>
        <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.20.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20.1">
          <times id="p1.1.m1.1.20.1.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20.1.1"/>
          <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.20.1.2.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20.1.2">
            <csymbol cd="latexml" id="p1.1.m1.1.20.1.2.1.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.1">bra</csymbol>
            <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.20.1.2.2.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20.1.2">
              <times id="p1.1.m1.1.20.1.2.2.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20.1.2.2.1"/>
              <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.2.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2">italic-ψ</ci>
              <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.4.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.4">italic-t</ci>
            </apply>
          </apply>
          <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.7.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7">italic-H</ci>
        </apply>
        <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20.2">
          <minus id="p1.1.m1.1.9.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.9"/>
          <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.1">
            <times id="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.1.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.1.1"/>
            <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.10.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.10">italic-i</ci>
            <csymbol cd="latexml" id="p1.1.m1.1.11.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.11">Planck-constant-over-2-pi</csymbol>
            <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.12.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.12">
              <divide id="p1.1.m1.1.12.1.cmml"/>
              <partialdiff id="p1.1.m1.1.12.2.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.12.2"/>
              <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.12.3.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.12.3">
                <partialdiff id="p1.1.m1.1.12.3.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.12.3.1"/>
                <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.12.3.2.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.12.3.2">italic-t</ci>
              </apply>
            </apply>
            <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.1.2.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.1.2">
              <csymbol cd="latexml" id="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.1.2.1.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.13">bra</csymbol>
              <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.1.2.2.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.1.2">
                <times id="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.1.2.2.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.20.2.1.2.2.1"/>
                <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.14.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.14">italic-ψ</ci>
                <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.16.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.16">italic-t</ci>
              </apply>
            </apply>
          </apply>
        </apply>
      </apply>
    </annotation-xml>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="p1.1.m1.1c">langlepsi(t)|H=-ihbar{partialoverpartial t}langlepsi(t)|.</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math>

Thus, the [[expected value]] of the observable ''G'' is conserved for any state of the system. In the case of the free particle, the conserved quantity is the [[angular momentum]].

== Hamilton's equations ==
[[William Rowan Hamilton|Hamilton]]'s equations in classical [[Hamiltonian mechanics]] have a direct analogy in quantum mechanics. Suppose we have a set of basis states <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="p1.1.m1.1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="left{left|nrightrangleright}" display="inline">
  <semantics id="p1.1.m1.1a">
    <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.6" xref="p1.1.m1.1.6.1.cmml">
      <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.1">{</mo>
      <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.6.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.6.2.1.cmml">
        <mo fence="true" id="p1.1.m1.1.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.6.2.1.1.cmml">|</mo>
        <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.3" xref="p1.1.m1.1.3.cmml">n</mi>
        <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.4" xref="p1.1.m1.1.6.2.1.1.cmml">⟩</mo>
      </mrow>
      <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.5">}</mo>
    </mrow>
    <annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="p1.1.m1.1b">
      <set id="p1.1.m1.1.6.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.6">
        <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.6.2.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.6.2">
          <csymbol cd="latexml" id="p1.1.m1.1.6.2.1.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2">ket</csymbol>
          <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.3.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.3">italic-n</ci>
        </apply>
      </set>
    </annotation-xml>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="p1.1.m1.1c">left{left|nrightrangleright}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math>, which need not necessarily be eigenstates of the energy. For simplicity, we assume that they are discrete, and that they are orthonormal, i.e.,

:<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="p1.1.m1.1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="langle n^{prime}|nrangle=delta_{nn^{prime}}." display="inline">
  <semantics id="p1.1.m1.1a">
    <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.11" xref="p1.1.m1.1.11.cmml">
      <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.11a" xref="p1.1.m1.1.11.cmml">
        <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.11.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.11.1.1.cmml">
          <mo stretchy="false" id="p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.11.1.1.1.cmml">⟨</mo>
          <msup id="p1.1.m1.1.11.1.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.11.1.1.cmml">
            <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2.cmml">n</mi>
            <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.3.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.3.1.cmml">′</mo>
          </msup>
          <mo stretchy="false" id="p1.1.m1.1.4" xref="p1.1.m1.1.11.1.1.1.cmml">|</mo>
          <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.5" xref="p1.1.m1.1.5.cmml">n</mi>
          <mo stretchy="false" id="p1.1.m1.1.6" xref="p1.1.m1.1.11.1.1.1.cmml">⟩</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.7" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.cmml">=</mo>
        <msub id="p1.1.m1.1.11.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.11.2.cmml">
          <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.8" xref="p1.1.m1.1.8.cmml">δ</mi>
          <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.9.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.cmml">
            <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.1.cmml">n</mi>
            <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.4" xref="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.4.cmml">⁢</mo>
            <msup id="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.5" xref="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.5.cmml">
              <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.2.cmml">n</mi>
              <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.3.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.3.1.cmml">′</mo>
            </msup>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mrow>
      <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.11b" xref="p1.1.m1.1.11.cmml">.</mo>
    </mrow>
    <annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="p1.1.m1.1b">
      <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.11.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.11">

              <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.3.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.9.1.3.1">′</ci>

        </apply>
      </apply>

    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="p1.1.m1.1c">langle n^{prime}|nrangle=delta_{nn^{prime}}.</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math>

Note that these basis states are assumed to be independent of time. We will assume that the Hamiltonian is also independent of time.

The instantaneous state of the system at time ''t'', <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="p1.1.m1.1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="left|psileft(tright)rightrangle" display="inline">
  <semantics id="p1.1.m1.1a">
    <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.7" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.cmml">
      <mo fence="true" id="p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.1.cmml">|</mo>
      <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.7.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.cmml">
        <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2.cmml">ψ</mi>
        <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.7.2.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.2.1.cmml">⁢</mo>
        <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.7.2.2">
          <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.3">(</mo>
          <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.4" xref="p1.1.m1.1.4.cmml">t</mi>
          <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.5">)</mo>
        </mrow>
      </mrow>
      <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.6" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.1.cmml">⟩</mo>
    </mrow>
    <annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="p1.1.m1.1b">
      <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7">
        <csymbol cd="latexml" id="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.1">ket</csymbol>
        <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.7.2.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7">
          <times id="p1.1.m1.1.7.2.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.2.1"/>
          <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.2.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2">italic-ψ</ci>
          <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.4.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.4">italic-t</ci>
        </apply>
      </apply>
    </annotation-xml>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="p1.1.m1.1c">left|psileft(tright)rightrangle</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math>, can be expanded in terms of these basis states:

:<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="p1.1.m1.1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="|psi(t)rangle=sum_{n}a_{n}(t)|nrangle" display="inline">
  <semantics id="p1.1.m1.1a">
    <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.18" xref="p1.1.m1.1.18.cmml">

        <mo fence="true" stretchy="false" id="p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.18.1.1.1.cmml">|</mo>

          <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2.cmml">ψ</mi>
          <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.18.1.2.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.18.1.2.1.cmml">⁢</mo>

            <mo stretchy="false" id="p1.1.m1.1.3">(</mo>

          </mrow>
        </mrow>
        <mo stretchy="false" id="p1.1.m1.1.6" xref="p1.1.m1.1.18.1.1.1.cmml">⟩</mo>

      <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.7" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.cmml">=</mo>
      <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.18.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.18.2.cmml">

          </msub>
          <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.18.2.2.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.18.2.2.1.cmml">⁢</mo>

            <mo stretchy="false" id="p1.1.m1.1.12">(</mo>

where

:<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="p1.1.m1.1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a_{n}(t)=langle n|psi(t)rangle." display="inline">
  <semantics id="p1.1.m1.1a">
    <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.16" xref="p1.1.m1.1.16.cmml">
      <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.16a" xref="p1.1.m1.1.16.cmml">
        <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.16.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.16.1.cmml">
          <msub id="p1.1.m1.1.16.1.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.16.1.2.cmml">
            <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml">a</mi>
            <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.2.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2.1.cmml">n</mi>
          </msub>
          <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.16.1.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.16.1.1.cmml">⁢</mo>
          <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.16.1.3">
            <mo stretchy="false" id="p1.1.m1.1.3">(</mo>

          <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.8" xref="p1.1.m1.1.8.cmml">n</mi>
          <mo stretchy="false" id="p1.1.m1.1.9" xref="p1.1.m1.1.16.2.1.1.cmml">|</mo>

    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="p1.1.m1.1c">a_{n}(t)=langle n|psi(t)rangle.</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math>

The coefficients ''a<sub>n</sub>(t)'' are [[complex number|complex]] variables. We can treat them as coordinates which specify the state of the system, like the position and momentum coordinates which specify a classical system. Like classical coordinates, they are generally not constant in time, and their time dependence gives rise to the time dependence of the system as a whole.

The expectation value of the Hamiltonian of this state, which is also the mean energy, is

:<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="p1.1.m1.1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="langle H(t)rangle stackrel{mathrm{def}}{=} langlepsi(t)|H|psi(t)%&#10;rangle=sum_{nn^{prime}}a_{n^{prime}}^{*}a_{n}langle n^{prime}|H|nrangle" display="inline">

    <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.7" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.cmml">
      <mo fence="true" id="p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.1.cmml">|</mo>
      <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.7.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.cmml">
        <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2.cmml">ψ</mi>

        <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.7.2.2">
          <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.3">(</mo>
          <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.4" xref="p1.1.m1.1.4.cmml">t</mi>
          <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.5">)</mo>
        </mrow>
      </mrow>
      <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.6" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.1.cmml">⟩</mo>
    </mrow>
    <annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="p1.1.m1.1b">
      <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7">
        <csymbol cd="latexml" id="p1.1.m1.1.7.1.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.1">ket</csymbol>
        <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.7.2.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7">
          <times id="p1.1.m1.1.7.2.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.7.2.1"/>
          <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.2.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2">italic-ψ</ci>
          <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.4.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.4">italic-t</ci>

      </apply>
    </annotation-xml>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="p1.1.m1.1c">left|psileft(tright)rightrangle</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math> in terms of the basis states.

Each of the ''a<sub>n</sub>(t)'''s actually corresponds to ''two'' independent degrees of freedom, since the variable has a real part and an imaginary part. We now perform the following trick: instead of using the real and imaginary parts as the independent variables, we use ''a<sub>n</sub>(t)'' and its [[complex conjugate]] ''a<sub>n</sub>*(t)''. With this choice of independent variables, we can calculate the [[partial derivative]]

:<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="p1.1.m1.1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="frac{partiallangle Hrangle}{partial a_{n^{prime}}^{*}}=sum_{n}a_{n}%&#10;langle n^{prime}|H|nrangle=langle n^{prime}|H|psirangle" display="inline">
  <semantics id="p1.1.m1.1a">

          <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.1.3" xref="p1.1.m1.1.10.1.cmml">

            <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.1.3a">⁡</mo>

        </mfrac>
        <mo id="p1.1.m1.1.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2.cmml">=</mo>

    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="p1.1.m1.1c">frac{partiallangle Hrangle}{partialpi_{n}}=frac{partial a_{n}}{%
partial t},quadfrac{partiallangle Hrangle}{partial a_{n}}=-frac{%
partialpi_{n}}{partial t}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math>

which is precisely the form of Hamilton's equations, with the <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="p1.1.m1.1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a_{n}" display="inline">
  <semantics id="p1.1.m1.1a">
    <msub id="p1.1.m1.1.3" xref="p1.1.m1.1.3.cmml">
      <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml">a</mi>
      <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.2.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2.1.cmml">n</mi>
    </msub>
    <annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="p1.1.m1.1b">
      <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.3.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.3">
        <csymbol cd="ambiguous" id="p1.1.m1.1.3.1.cmml">subscript</csymbol>
        <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.1">italic-a</ci>
        <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.2.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2.1">italic-n</ci>
      </apply>
    </annotation-xml>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="p1.1.m1.1c">a_{n}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math>s as the generalized coordinates, the <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="p1.1.m1.1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="pi_{n}" display="inline">
  <semantics id="p1.1.m1.1a">
    <msub id="p1.1.m1.1.3" xref="p1.1.m1.1.3.cmml">
      <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml">π</mi>
      <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.2.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2.1.cmml">n</mi>
    </msub>
    <annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="p1.1.m1.1b">
      <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.3.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.3">
        <csymbol cd="ambiguous" id="p1.1.m1.1.3.1.cmml">subscript</csymbol>
        <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.1">italic-π</ci>
        <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.2.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2.1">italic-n</ci>
      </apply>
    </annotation-xml>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="p1.1.m1.1c">pi_{n}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math>s as the conjugate momenta, and <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="p1.1.m1.1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="langle Hrangle" display="inline">
  <semantics id="p1.1.m1.1a">
    <mrow id="p1.1.m1.1.4" xref="p1.1.m1.1.4.1.cmml">
      <mo stretchy="false" id="p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="p1.1.m1.1.4.1.1.cmml">⟨</mo>
      <mi id="p1.1.m1.1.2" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2.cmml">H</mi>
      <mo stretchy="false" id="p1.1.m1.1.3" xref="p1.1.m1.1.4.1.1.cmml">⟩</mo>
    </mrow>
    <annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="p1.1.m1.1b">
      <apply id="p1.1.m1.1.4.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.4">
        <csymbol cd="latexml" id="p1.1.m1.1.4.1.1.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.1">delimited-⟨⟩</csymbol>
        <ci id="p1.1.m1.1.2.cmml" xref="p1.1.m1.1.2">italic-H</ci>
      </apply>
    </annotation-xml>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="p1.1.m1.1c">langle Hrangle</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math> taking the place of the classical Hamiltonian.
